========================================
TITLE: Unit 1 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Use basic phrases

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je suis Marie.
English:     I am Marie.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      C'est un chat.
English:     It's a cat.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Un chat mange.
English:     A cat is eating.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Paul mange un croissant.
English:     Paul is eating a croissant.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu es Marc ?
English:     Are you Marc?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Non, je suis Paul.
English:     No, I am Paul.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Gender
In French, all nouns are either masculine or feminine . Masculine nouns use un , and feminine nouns use une .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      un garçon
English:     a boy
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      une fille
English:     a girl
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      un homme
English:     a man
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      une femme
English:     a woman
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      un chien
English:     a dog
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      une pizza
English:     a pizza
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
I think, therefore...
In English, we say I am but you are . In French, you do the same thing!

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( être )            
je I                      | suis am                  
tu you                    | es are                   
il / elle he / she        | est is                   
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je suis un garçon.
English:     Iama boy.
----------------------


==================== END OF FILE 1 ====================

========================================
TITLE: Unit 2 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Greet people

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Bonjour, comment ça va ?
English:     Good morning, how are you doing?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ça va très bien, et toi ?
English:     I am doing very well, and you?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ça va.
English:     I am fine.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Au revoir, Marie.
English:     Goodbye, Marie.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Au revoir, bonne journée.
English:     Goodbye, have a good day.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Merci beaucoup.
English:     Thank you very much.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Accents
In French, an accent mark over a letter can make a new sound.
j e j e (as in "p e tition")
é journ é e (similar to "b ay ")
è tr è s (as in "b e t")
If the last letter of a word is an e (without an accent!), it's usually silent.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      femme
English:     woman
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      bonne nuit
English:     good night
----------------------


==================== END OF FILE 2 ====================

========================================
TITLE: Unit 3 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Introduce yourself

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Excuse-moi, tu parles français ?
English:     Excuse me, do you speak French?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Oui, je suis français.
English:     Yes, I am French.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Comment tu t'appelles ?
English:     What is your name?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je m'appelle Julia.
English:     My name is Julia.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je parle espagnol.
English:     I speak Spanish.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je suis américaine.
English:     I am American.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Verbs
English verbs don't change that much. For example, we say I run , you run , he runs , and so on. But French verbs change a lot!

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( parler )          
je I                      | parl e speak             
tu you                    | parl es speak            
il / elle he / she        | parl e speaks            
-------------
But don't be fooled! The s in parle s is actually silent, so all these forms are pronounced the same!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je parle. Tu parles.
English:     I speak. You speak.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Gender
In French, adjectives can look different depending on the gender of what they describe. Normally, feminine adjectives end in e .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Gabriel est espagnol.
English:     Gabriel is Spanish.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Sarah est espagnole.
English:     Sarah is Spanish.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il est américain.
English:     He is American.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elle est américaine.
English:     She is American.
----------------------
Sometimes the extra e changes the sound a little, so listen carefully!


==================== END OF FILE 3 ====================

========================================
TITLE: Unit 4 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Use the present tense

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Marie habite en Italie.
English:     Marie lives in Italy.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Marie est journaliste.
English:     Marie is a journalist.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'étudie à New York, et toi ?
English:     I am studying in New York, and you?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je travaille à Paris.
English:     I work in Paris.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je suis en Europe.
English:     I am in Europe.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'habite avec Marie.
English:     I live with Marie.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
J'habite à Paris !
French has two words for in . You'll use à with cities but en with many countries.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'habite à Paris.
English:     I live in Paris.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'habite en France.
English:     I live in France.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je travaille à Madrid.
English:     I work in Madrid.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je travaille en Espagne.
English:     I work in Spain.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je travaille en France.​
English:     I work in France.
----------------------


==================== END OF FILE 4 ====================

========================================
TITLE: Unit 5 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Get around town

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Où est le restaurant, s'il vous plaît ?
English:     Where is the restaurant, please?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je vais à la gare.
English:     I am going to the train station.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu as une valise ?
English:     Do you have a suitcase?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je vais à Paris en voiture.
English:     I am going to Paris by car.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je prends le train et l'avion.
English:     I am taking the train and the plane.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      C'est un restaurant mexicain.
English:     It is a Mexican restaurant.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
The, the, or the?
Le goes with masculine nouns .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      le garçon
English:     the boy
----------------------
La goes with feminine ones.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      la femme
English:     the woman
----------------------
But if the word starts with a vowel or silent h , use l' instead!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      l'homme
English:     the man
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Tu as un passeport ?
Most French verbs change really predictably. But some verbs just do their own thing and don't follow typical patterns.

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( aller )           
je I                      | vais go                  
tu you                    | vas go                   
il / elle he / she        | va goes                  
-------------
If a verb begins with a vowel , be sure to change je to j' !

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( avoir )           
j' I                      | ai have                  
tu you                    | as have                  
il / elle he / she        | a has                    
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'ai un passeport.
English:     I have a passport.
----------------------


==================== END OF FILE 5 ====================

========================================
TITLE: Unit 6 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Refer to family members

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ton père habite ici ?
English:     Does your father live here?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Non, mon père habite en Espagne.
English:     No, my father lives in Spain.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ma famille habite en France.
English:     My family lives in France.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Le mari de Julia est mexicain.
English:     Julia's husband is Mexican.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Mon père a un chat.
English:     My father has a cat.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'ai un animal de compagnie.
English:     I have a pet.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Ma famille !
In English we say my mother and my father . In French you'd say mon père and ma mère , because words like my and your change based on the gender of the word after them!

--- Table ---
masculine                 | feminine                 
mon père my father        | ma mère my mother        
ton frère your brother    | ta sœur your sister      
son fils his / her son    | sa fille his / her daughter
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      mon père
English:     my father
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Whose kid is this?
In English, we say Marie 's cat . But in French, you'd switch the word order and say le chat de Marie.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      le chat de Marie
English:     Marie's cat
----------------------
Before vowels , de becomes d' .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      le chien d'Anna
English:     Anna's dog
----------------------

========================================
TITLE: Unit 7 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Talk about things you do

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous mangeons un croissant.
English:     We are eating a croissant.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'étudie la musique.
English:     I am studying music.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu aimes le chocolat ?
English:     Do you like chocolate?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous allons au cinéma.
English:     We are going to the movie theater.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu vas à l'école ?
English:     Are you going to school?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Non, je vais au parc.
English:     No, I'm going to the park.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Au wow!
In French, à and le are never used together. Instead, they combine into au !

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu vas au restaurant.
English:     You are going to the restaurant.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elle va au zoo.
English:     She is going to the zoo.
----------------------


==================== END OF FILE 7 ====================

========================================
TITLE: Unit 8 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Form the plural

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Les professeurs habitent ici.
English:     The professors live here.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous avons deux filles.
English:     We have two daughters.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elles travaillent en Angleterre.
English:     They work in England.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Sarah a trois chats.
English:     Sarah has three cats.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ils étudient le français.
English:     They study French.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il a beaucoup de chiens.
English:     He has a lot of dogs.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Plural
Talking about more than one thing in French works just like in English — just add s ! But in French, that plural s is usually silent.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      un chat
English:     one cat
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      deux chats
English:     two cats
----------------------
Also, le , la and l' become les .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      les garçons
English:     the boys
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Ils and elles
Ils and elles both mean they . Use elles for groups of only women, and use ils for groups of men or mixed groups.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ils sont étudiants.
English:     They are students.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elles sont étudiantes.
English:     They are students.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Let’s talk about Present Tense!
All verbs change depending on if you’re talking about je , tu , and so on!

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( parler )          
je                        | parl e                   
tu                        | parl es                  
il / elle                 | parl e                   
nous                      | parl ons                 
vous                      | parl ez                  
ils / elles               | parl ent                 
-------------


==================== END OF FILE 8 ====================

========================================
TITLE: Unit 9 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Describe your family

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ce sont mes parents.
English:     These are my parents.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Mes sœurs sont étudiantes.
English:     My sisters are students.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Mon père est amusant.
English:     My father is funny.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Mes parents sont américains.
English:     My parents are American.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ma fille est intelligente.
English:     My daughter is intelligent.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Adjectives
If you're talking about a plural noun , add s to the adjective too!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      La femme est contente.
English:     The woman is happy.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Les femmes sont contentes.
English:     The women are happy.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
J'aime mes parents !
In English, we say my brother and my brothers . But in French, if you have more than one brother, words like my and your change!

--- Table ---
singular                  | plural                   
mon frère my brother      | mes frère s my brothers  
ta sœur your sister       | tes sœur s your sisters  
sa voiture his/her car    | ses voiture s his/her cars
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      le garçon et ses parents
English:     the boy and his parents
----------------------

TITLE: Unit 10 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Order food and drink

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu veux une bière ?
English:     Do you want a beer?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Non, je voudrais un verre de vin.
English:     No, I would like a glass of wine.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      OK, et tu prends un sandwich ou une pizza ?
English:     Okay, and are you having a sandwich or a pizza?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je voudrais un dessert.
English:     I would like a dessert.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      L'addition, s'il vous plaît !
English:     The check, please!
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Une table pour deux personnes, s'il vous plaît.
English:     One table for two people, please.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Je voudrais un verre d'eau !
D'oh! Remember, if a noun begins with a vowel , you use d' instead of de . It makes the words run a little smoother!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      une bouteille d'eau
English:     a bottle of water
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      un fromage d'Italie
English:     a cheese from Italy
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      quatre verres d'eau
English:     four glasses of water
----------------------

========================================
TITLE: Unit 1 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Use gender and number agreement

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Le restaurant est ouvert.
English:     The restaurant is open.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      La maison est petite.
English:     The house is small.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Le magasin est fermé aujourd'hui.
English:     The store is closed today.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Les magasins sont grands.
English:     The stores are big.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Un vélo vert !
French adjectives usually come after the noun they're describing. So, a green bike would be un vélo vert .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      une université française
English:     aFrenchuniversity
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      le thé vert
English:     thegreentea
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      le restaurant mexicain
English:     theMexicanrestaurant
----------------------


==================== END OF FILE 11 ====================

========================================
TITLE: Unit 2 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Discuss destinations

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu voyages avec ta sœur ?
English:     Are you traveling with your sister?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Oui, nous visitons le Japon.
English:     Yes, we are visiting Japan.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu vas à la plage ?
English:     Are you going to the beach?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Non, je visite un château.
English:     No, I am visiting a castle.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elles voyagent beaucoup.
English:     They travel a lot.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il visite les États-Unis.
English:     He is visiting the United States.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
J'aime la France !
In English, saying The trains are big or I like the wine usually means you're talking about a particular wine or specific trains. In French, you use le , la , or les when talking about specific things, but you also use these words when stating general facts!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Les trains sont grands.
English:     Trains are big.
----------------------
You also use them when talking about your likes or dislikes.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu aimes le vin ?
English:     Do you like wine?
----------------------
And also when talking about countries!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Le Mexique est mon pays.
English:     Mexico is my country.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Aux my goodness!
We've already seen that au is a combination of à and le . Now, if the noun is plural , use aux , instead of à les .
à + le = au à + les = aux
Here are some examples that use these contractions .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu vas au supermarché ?
English:     You are goingto thesupermarket.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je vais aux Etats‑Unis.
English:     I am goingto theUnited States.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il va aux toilettes.
English:     He is goingto thebathrooms.​
----------------------

========================================
TITLE: Unit 3 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Describe your home

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ma maison a quatre pièces.
English:     My house has four rooms.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il y a des fleurs dans le jardin.
English:     There are flowers in the garden.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous aimons les fleurs.
English:     We like flowers.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tes voisins sont gentils.
English:     Your neighbors are kind.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il y a un cheval dans ton appartement !
English:     There is a horse in your apartment!
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
That's some word!
Un and une become des when you are talking about more than one thing. In English, we can just say cats , but in French you have to say des chats .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      un arbre
English:     a tree
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      des arbres
English:     trees
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      une lettre
English:     a letter
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      des lettres
English:     letters
----------------------

TITLE: Unit 4 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Describe where you work

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il y a un ordinateur dans le bureau.
English:     There is a computer in the office.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Marie est ma collègue.
English:     Marie is my colleague.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      C'est une usine française.
English:     It's a French factory.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je travaille à la maison.
English:     I work at home.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Mon bureau est grand.
English:     My office is big.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Tu écris une lettre ?
Notice that écrire adds a v for some endings!

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( écrire )          
j' I                      | écris write              
tu you                    | écris write              
il / elle he / she        | écrit writes             
ils / elles they          | écri v ent write         
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il écrit un message.
English:     He is writing a message.
----------------------


==================== END OF FILE 14 ====================

========================================
TITLE: Unit 5 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Talk about food

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu prépares le repas ?
English:     Are you making the meal?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Oui, c'est un plat français.
English:     Yes this is a French dish.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Cette pizza est prête.
English:     This pizza is ready.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu prends le petit déjeuner ?
English:     Are you having breakfast?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous préparons le café.
English:     We are making coffee.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Cette banane est bonne.
English:     This banana is good.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Verbs
Verbs that end in ‑er , like aim er and mang er , generally follow the same ending pattern!

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( préparer )        
je I                      | prépar e prepare         
tu you                    | prépar es prepare        
il / elle he / she        | prépar e prepares        
nous we                   | prépar ons prepare       
ils / elles they          | prépar ent prepare       
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous préparons un gâteau.
English:     We are making a cake.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
What's this?
The word for this in French changes depending on the gender of the noun it's with!

--- Table ---
masculine                 | feminine                 
ce plat this plate        | cette pomme this apple   
-------------
But the word these never changes!

--- Table ---
masculine                 | feminine                 
ces plats these plates    | ces pommes these apples  
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ces salades sont bonnes.
English:     These salads are good.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Let's talk about Agreement!
All adjectives and words like my , your , and so on, change based on the noun they describe.​

========================================
TITLE: Unit 6 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Use the present tense

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu lis souvent ?
English:     Do you read often?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Oui, je lis chaque soir.
English:     Yes, I read every evening.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous écoutons souvent la radio.
English:     We often listen to the radio.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ce matin, elle prend le petit déjeuner au lit !
English:     This morning, she's having breakfast in bed!
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Aujourd'hui, c'est mercredi.
English:     Today, it's Wednesday.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il regarde la télé chaque jour.
English:     He watches TV every day.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
It's the afternoon!
In French, make sure you include the le , la , or l' when talking about the time of day or meals!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      C'est l'après‑midi.
English:     It's afternoon.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      après le dessert
English:     after dessert
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      après le dîner
English:     after dinner
----------------------

========================================
TITLE: Unit 7 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Shop for clothes

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ça coûte combien ?
English:     How much does it cost?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      La robe coûte cinq euros.
English:     The dress costs five euros.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      C'est cher.
English:     It's expensive.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu achètes des vêtements ?
English:     Are you buying clothes?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Oui, j'achète une veste.
English:     Yes, I'm buying a jacket.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je veux un pantalon blanc.
English:     I want white pants.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Gender
Remember, remember, the noun and its gender ! Some adjectives take a special form with feminine nouns.

--- Table ---
masculine                 | feminine                 
blanc                     | blan che                 
cher                      | ch ère                   
bon                       | bon ne                   
gentil                    | gentil le                
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      un T‑shirt cher
English:     an expensive T‑shirt
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      une robe chère
English:     an expensive dress
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
With our powers combined!
Remember how à combines with le to make au ? The word de can also combine with le and les to form something new.
de + le = du de + les = des
Here are some examples that use these contractions .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      le prix du sac
English:     the priceof thebag
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      le prix des oranges
English:     the priceof theoranges
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      le prix des robes
English:     the priceof thedresses
----------------------

========================================
TITLE: Unit 8 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Exchange personal information

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous ne parlons pas français.
English:     We do not speak French.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu viens d'Espagne ?
English:     Do you come from Spain?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Non, je viens du Mexique.
English:     No, I come from Mexico.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Quel âge as-tu ?
English:     How old are you?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'ai treize ans.
English:     I am thirteen years old.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Tu n'es pas français !
In English, we'd say I am not Italian or He is not American . But in French you need two words to say not , like a negative sandwich!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je ne suis pas italien.
English:     I amnotItalian.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous ne parlons pas espagnol.
English:     We donotspeak Spanish.
----------------------
If the verb begins with a vowel , ne becomes n' .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu n'es pas canadien.
English:     You arenotCanadian.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il n'est pas jeune.
English:     He isnotyoung.
----------------------
In informal conversations with French speakers, you might notice that they don't always use ne . For example, you'll often hear Il est pas jeune instead of Il n' est pas jeune.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il ne parle pas japonais.
English:     He doesnotspeak Japanese.
----------------------

des ponts danger eux      | des rues danger euses

KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Ask people about themselves

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Alice et Paul, vous cuisinez ?
English:     Alice and Paul, do you cook?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---

----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Marc et Julia, ce sont vos parents ?
English:     Marc and Julia, are these your parents?
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Vous
In English we say you , no matter whether we're talking to one person or one hundred. But in French, tu is specifically for one person!
For two or more, use vous , and make sure the verb ends in ‑ez . You can think of vous as the French y'all !

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      vous mangez
English:     you all eat
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      vous parlez
English:     you all speak
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      vous cuisinez
English:     you all cook
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      vous habitez
English:     you all live
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Vous voulez des bananes ?
English:     Do you want some bananas?
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Mon amie !
You've seen that you use ma , ta , and sa before feminine nouns .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      ma sœur
English:     my sister
----------------------
But if the noun starts with a vowel , you'll need to use mon , ton , or son instead.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      mon amie
English:     my friend
----------------------

TITLE: Unit 12 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Tell time

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu dors à midi ?
English:     You sleep at noon?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il est huit heures du soir.
English:     It's eight o'clock at night.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il est neuf heures du matin.
English:     It's nine o'clock in the morning.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il est tard.
English:     It's late.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je dois rentrer avant minuit.
English:     I have to go home before midnight.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
What time is it?
To say what time it is in French, start your sentence with Il est !

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il est trois heures et quart.
English:     It's a quarter past three.
----------------------
In English, we can say It's four o'clock or simply It's four , but in French, you always need to include heures if you're telling the time.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il est sept heures.
English:     It's seven o'clock.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Let's talk about Present Tense!
Watch out for irregular verb patterns:​​
If there are two verbs, make sure the second is the form ending in ‑er , ‑ir , or ‑re .​​

Talk to someone formally

Good day, sir!
There are two ways to say you in French! In general, you use tu in friendly conversations or with kids. You can use vous to address more than one person, but also in formal situations or with adults you don't know.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu aimes le vin ?

English:     Ma'am, doyouwant some coffee?

TIP

Which what is which?
To ask a what or which question, you'll use quel if the noun is masculine and quelle if it's feminine.

English:     Whichtrain is going to Paris?

Talk about hobbies

TIP
------------------------------
No more silence!
A lot of consonants at the end of French words are silent. But if the next word begins with a vowel or a silent h , it is silent no more!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      les
English:     the
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      les enfants
English:     the children
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      grand
English:     big
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      grand arbre
English:     big tree
----------------------
Notice how the s sounds like a z , while the d sounds like a t .
There are exceptions! For example, the t in e t is never pronounced.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je pars et il arrive.

Describe your breakfast

--- Example Phrase ---

Du thé ou du café ?
Some nouns are uncountable — you don't put a number before them. For example, we generally say I want some honey , not I want one honey .
In French, you always need du , de la , or des before those uncountable nouns!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je prends du sucre avec mon café.
English:     I take sugar with my coffee.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'achète des pâtes.
English:     I buy pasta.

--- Example Phrase ---

English:     Do you want some wine?

TIP
------------------------------
J'adore le chocolat !
Remember, when you're talking about things you like (or don't like!), you should always use le , la , or les .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il adore le chocolat.
English:     He loves chocolate.

TITLE: Unit 17 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Talk about school

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Est-ce que tu aimes le français ?
English:     Do you like French?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Oui, j'apprends le français à l'université.
English:     Yes, I'm learning French at the university.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      C'est facile ou c'est difficile ?
English:     Is it easy or is it difficult?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Les examens sont difficiles.
English:     The exams are difficult.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Vous pouvez parler plus lentement ?
English:     Can you speak more slowly?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Les élèves comprennent.
English:     The students understand.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Je ne comprends pas !
All verbs that end in ‑prendre (like ap prendre and com prendre ) use the same pattern of verb endings! Let's use prendre as a guide:

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( prendre )         
je I                      | pren ds take             
tu you                    | pren ds take             
il / elle he / she        | pren d takes             
nous we                   | pren ons take            
vous you all              | pren ez take             
ils / elles they          | pren nent take           
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Les élèves comprennent.
English:     The students understand.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Do you do that in French?
In English, we can use do or does to make a question, like Do you love me? In French, you can begin questions with Est‑ce que … !

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Est‑ce que tu veux du lait ?
English:     Doyou want some milk?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Est‑ce qu'Anne comprend ?
English:     DoesAnne understand?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Est‑ce que vous voyagez ensemble ?
English:     Doyou travel together?
----------------------

TITLE: Unit 18 Guidebook

KEY PHRASES

Share work schedules

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Vous finissez la réunion maintenant ?
English:     Are you finishing the meeting now?

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Oui. C'est la troisième réunion aujourd'hui, j'ai besoin d'un café.
English:     Yes. This is the third meeting today; I need a coffee.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---

English:     She finishes late today.

English:     We choose our schedule.

English:     I have a meeting at eight o'clock.

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Let me finish!
A lot of verbs that end in ‑ir will have the same set of word endings. Let's use fin ir as a guide!

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( finir )           
je I                      | fin is finish            
tu you                    | fin is finish            
il / elle he / she        | fin it finishes          
nous we                   | fin issons finish        
vous you all              | fin issez finish         
ils / elles they          | fin issent finish        
-------------
Notice that for verbs like finir , the s is doubled with nous , vous , and ils / elles !

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je finis mon travail.
English:     I finish my work.
----------------------

Adjectives
We've seen that French adjectives usually come after the noun . But in some cases the adjective actually comes first!
This applies to adjectives that are talking about… B eauty! A ge! G oodness! S ize!
 ... BAGS !

--- Example Phrase ---

English:     They prefer chocolate.​​

TITLE: Unit 20 Guidebook

Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Describe your routine

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      D'habitude, tu te réveilles à quelle heure ?
English:     Usually, what time do you wake up?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      D'habitude, je me réveille très tôt.
English:     Usually, I wake up very early.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Que fais-tu le matin ?
English:     What do you do in the morning?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je fais du sport le matin.
English:     I exercise in the morning.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Et que prends-tu au petit déjeuner ?
English:     And what do you have at breakfast?

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Le matin, je ne mange pas.
English:     In the morning, I don't eat.

TIP
------------------------------
Je me réveille toujours tard !
Remember that little m' in phrases like Je m' appelle Charlotte ? It literally means I call myself Charlotte .

--- Table ---
subject pronoun           | reflexive pronoun        
je                        | me                       
tu                        | te                       
il / elle                 | se                       
nous                      | nous                     
vous                      | vous                     
ils / elles               | se                       
-------------
Lots of French verbs add pronouns like me and te , even when we wouldn't say myself or yourself in English!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Le matin, je me réveille tôt.
English:     In the morning, I wake up early.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il se couche tard.
English:     He goes to bed late.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ils se préparent vite.
English:     They get ready quickly.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous nous réveillons tard.
English:     We get up late.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Body language
In English, we say He brushes his teeth or I wash my face , but in French you'd normally use le , la , or les instead of my or his before parts of the body.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elle se brosse les cheveux.
English:     She brushes her hair.
----------------------

Describe people

--- Example Phrase ---

English:     You are stressed because you are working too much.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---

TIP
------------------------------
Sors avec moi !

--- Example Phrase ---

--- Example Phrase ---

--- Example Phrase ---

Celui‑ci ou celui‑là ?
In French, when you say I want this one or You need that one! , the word you choose depends on the noun's gender and number !

--- Table ---
masculine                 | feminine                 
celui‑ci , celui‑là this one, that one | celle‑ci , celle‑là this one, that one
ceux‑ci , ceux‑là these ones, those ones | celles‑ci , celles‑là these ones, those ones

English:     Adults have to get up early to work.

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
That's not faire!
The verb faire is a little different from other ‑re verbs when it comes to vous , ils , and elles .

--- Table ---
verb lire                 | verb faire               
je lis                    | je fais                  
tu lis                    | tu fais                  
il / elle lit             | il / elle fait           
nous lisons               | nous faisons             
vous lisez                | vous faites              
ils / elles lisent        | ils / elles font         
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ils font un gâteau pour le dessert.​
English:     They are making a cake for dessert.​
----------------------

TIP
------------------------------
Let's talk about Reflexives!
Certain verbs need reflexive pronouns like me , te , etc. before them.​​

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu dois te brosser les dents!​
English:     You should brush your teeth!​​
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous ne nous réveillons pas tôt.​
English:     We don’t wake up early.​​
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Tu me comprends ?
In English, words like me come after the verb (for example, Can you hear me ? ), but in French they come before the verb!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elle me parle.
English:     She is talkingto me.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elle te parle.
English:     She is talkingto you.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elle nous parle.
English:     She is talkingto us.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elle vous parle.
English:     She is talkingto you (all).
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Mes amis me connaissent bien.
English:     My friends knowmewell.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Je sais que c'est ton anniversaire !
In English, we might say I don't know where the hotel is . French is very similar! But you put the verb right after words where , when , etc.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Vous savez où est l'hôtel ?
English:     Do you know where the hotel is?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Vous savez à quelle heure est le petit déjeuner ?
English:     Do you know what time breakfast is?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous savons quand part le train.
English:     We know when the train is leaving.
----------------------

Four twenties?

Je suis en train de dormir...
In English, when we're in the middle of a meal, we'll say I am eating . In French, you can say Je suis en train de manger to express that you're doing something in the moment.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je suis en train de partir.
English:     I am leaving.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Vous êtes en train de manger.
English:     You are eating.
----------------------
Notice that after en train de , you'll need to use the infinitive — the form of the verb that ends with ‑er , ‑ir , or ‑re .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il est en train de prendre une douche.
English:     He is taking a shower.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Asseyez‑vous sur cette chaise.
English:     Sit on this chair.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Lève‑toi de cette chaise !
English:     Get up off this chair!
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Assieds‑toi sur cette chaise !​
English:     Sit on this chair!

What have you done?!

Who's on first?
In French, le rez‑de‑chaussée is the ground floor. Le premier étage is actually the floor above that.

English:     Claudia is on the ground floor.

KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Use the imperfect

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Papa, tu étais vraiment jeune sur cette photo.
English:     Dad, you were really young in this photo.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Oui ! Quand j'étais jeune, j'étudiais à Bordeaux.
English:     Yes! When I was young, I was studying in Bordeaux.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Mon grand-père était en France dans les années soixante.
English:     My grandfather was in France in the sixties.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      C'était mieux avant.
English:     It was better before.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Quand j'étais petite, j'habitais en Italie.
English:     When I was little, I was living in Italy.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je travaillais à New York.
English:     I was working in New York.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
I was an imparfait student
We've already seen one way to talk about the past in French: the passé composé .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'ai acheté une maison.
English:     I bought a house.
----------------------
But if you want to describe something you used to do or how something used to be, you'll use a verb form called imparfait .
Let's start by looking at the je , tu , and il / elle forms.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Quand j'étais à l'université, j'étudiais le français.
English:     When I was in college, I studied French.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Quand tu étais étudiant, tu habitais à Paris.
English:     When you were a student, you were living in Paris.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Quand il était jeune, il aimait étudier.
English:     When he was young, he loved studying.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je travaillais à Paris.
English:     I worked in Paris.
----------------------


==================== END OF FILE 50 ====================

========================================
TITLE: Unit 19 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Talk about recent events

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Le mois dernier, elle est allée en Italie.
English:     Last month, she went to Italy.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Marie et Alice sont allées au cinéma.
English:     Marie and Alice went to the movie theater.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Hier, les enfants ont joué dans le jardin.
English:     Yesterday, the children played in the garden.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ce musée était intéressant et pas cher.
English:     That museum was interesting and inexpensive.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      La semaine dernière, il faisait très beau.
English:     Last week, it was very nice.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il est allé à la plage la semaine dernière.
English:     He went to the beach last week.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
I am arrived!
We've already seen how to use avoir plus a verb to talk about the past, like J' ai visit é .
But for some verbs that express movement (like aller and arriver ), you'll need être instead of avoir .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je suis allé en vacances au Japon.
English:     I went on vacation to Japan.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu es arrivé au bureau.
English:     You arrived at the office.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il est allé au Maroc.
English:     He went to Morocco.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Elle est allée en Belgique
Unlike verbs using avoir in the past, verbs that use être change depending on the gender and number of who you're talking about

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Julia, tu es allée au supermarché ?
English:     Julia, you went to the supermarket?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elles sont arrivées à la maison.
English:     They arrived at the house.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous sommes allés au Sénégal.
English:     We went to Senegal.
----------------------
Remember, the ‑e and ‑s are silent!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elle est allée au cinéma avec ses amis.
English:     She went to the movies with her friends.
----------------------

========================================
TITLE: Unit 20 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Make offers and requests

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Vous nous aidez à laver les légumes ?
English:     Can you help us wash the vegetables?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je nettoie la table ?
English:     Should I clean the table?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ils n'entendent jamais le téléphone.
English:     They never hear the phone.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu m'appelles bientôt ?
English:     Will you call me soon?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      D'accord, je t'appelle ce soir.
English:     Okay, I'll call you tonight.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      On mange ensemble la semaine prochaine ?
English:     Will we eat together next week?
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Tu m'aides à ranger ?
To be polite in English, we often use can or should , like in Can you give that to me? or Should I help with dinner? In French, you can just state your request or offer as a question.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je prépare le dessert ?
English:     Should I prepare the dessert?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu mets des assiettes sur la table ?
English:     Can you put plates on the table?
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Le train part dans une heure !
Je t'appelle by itself can mean I'm calling you right now. But if you add a word like demain , it means I will call you!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      On mange ensemble demain ?
English:     Will we eat together tomorrow?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      On se voit la semaine prochaine ?
English:     Will we see each other next week?
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Let's talk about commands!
To tell someone to do something, simply drop the tu or vous !
For ‑er verbs , you must also drop the ‑s from the tu form.

Duo t'attend...
Verbs like attend re , entend re , and vend re have the same endings!

--- Table ---
verb attendre             | verb entendre            
j'attend s                | j'entend s               
tu attend s               | tu entend s              
il / elle attend          | il / elle entend         
nous attend ons           | nous entend ons          
vous attend ez            | vous entend ez           
ils / elles attend ent    | ils / elles entend ent

TITLE: Unit 2 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Describe your weekend

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Vous avez passé le week-end ensemble ?
English:     Did you spend the weekend together?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Oui, nous avons passé le week-end dans une maison près de la mer.
English:     Yes, we spent the weekend in a house near the sea.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Vous avez invité qui ?
English:     Who did you invite?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous avons invité nos amis.
English:     We invited our friends.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Vous avez nagé ?
English:     Did you swim?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Oui, j'ai nagé dans ma piscine.
English:     Yes, I swam in my pool.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Je marche jusqu'à la plage
To say that you went up to a place but didn't go inside, use jusqu'à . When you want to say that you went to a place and then went inside, use à .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'ai marché jusqu'au restaurant.
English:     I walked to the restaurant (but didn't go in).
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je suis allé au restaurant.
English:     I went to the restaurant (and had a meal!).
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Let’s talk about Past Tense!
To talk about past actions and say things like I talked , follow this pattern:

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( parler )          
j'                        | ai parl é                
tu                        | as parl é                
il / elle                 | a parl é                 
nous                      | avons parl é             
vous                      | avez parl é              
ils / elles               | ont parl é               
-------------

Describe people you know

--- Example Phrase ---

English:     Is she your cousin ?

C'est un danseur
Use c'est when you need words like un , ma , etc. before the noun .

----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---

English:     She's nice.

--- Example Phrase ---

----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je vais emprunter ce livre à la bibliothèque.
English:     I'm going to borrow this book from the library.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Tu l'as vu ?
We've seen that tu le vois means you see it . To say the same thing in the past, you'll say tu l' as vu .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Le dernier film d'Isabelle Huppert ? Je l'ai vu hier.
English:     Isabelle Huppert's last film? I sawityesterday.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Le Comte de Monte‑Cristo ? Je l'ai lu trois fois.
English:     The Count of Monte‑Cristo? I readitthree times.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'ai adoré ce livre ! Tu l'as emprunté à la bibliothèque ?
English:     I loved this book! Did you borrowitfrom the library?
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Let’s talk about motion verbs!
When talking about the past, verbs of motion use être instead of avoir . If the subject is feminine , add an ‑e . If the subject is plural , add an ‑s !

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( aller)            
je                        | suis all é(e)            
tu                        | es all é(e)              
il / elle                 | est all é(e)             
nous                      | sommes all é(e)s         
vous                      | êtes all é(e)s           
ils / elles               | sont all é(e)s           
-------------

TITLE: Unit 11 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Use indirect object pronouns

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu me donnes quoi ?
English:     What are you giving me?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      La directrice ne m'écoute pas quand je lui parle.
English:     The director doesn't listen to me when I'm speaking to her.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je dois lui écrire un e-mail mais mon clavier a un problème.
English:     I have to write an email to him, but my keyboard has a problem.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ces employés sont nouveaux et je leur montre les bureaux.
English:     These employees are new, and I'm showing the offices to them.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Cette employée est nouvelle alors je lui présente les autres membres de l'équipe.
English:     This employee is new, so I'm introducing the other team members to her.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Send me a postcard!
We've seen how to use le or la to say things like Elle le voit and Elle la voit .
To say to him , to her , or to it , you'll use lui instead. Keep in mind that some French verbs use à when we wouldn't use to in English!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elle écrit une lettre à Jean.
English:     She writes a letterto Jean.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elle lui écrit une lettre.
English:     She writes a letterto him.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elle répond à Sylvie.
English:     She answersSylvie.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Elle lui répond.
English:     She answersher.
----------------------
Notice that the à disappears as well when you use lui .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Il lui écrit une lettre.
English:     He writes a letterto him.
----------------------

------------------------------
Tu pars ?
Verbs like partir , sortir , dormir and servir will all have similar endings.

--- Table ---
verb partir               | verb dormir              
je par s                  | je dor s                 
tu par s                  | tu dor s                 
il/elle par t             | il/elle dor t            
nous part ons             | nous dorm ons            
vous part ez              | vous dorm ez             
ils/elles part ent        | ils/elles dorm ent       
-------------
They have the same endings in the passé composé as well!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je suis parti en retard.
English:     I left late.

--- Example Phrase ---

English:     I slept at the hotel.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Le restaurant sert des pizzas froides !

Share travel experiences

On y va
Just like en , lui , les , and leur , y comes before the verb .

--- Example Phrase ---

English:     What time are you going to the restaurant? I'm going around 8 o'clock.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      On y va !
English:     Let's go!

--- Example Phrase ---

English:     Let's go!

TITLE: Unit 16 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Talk about technology

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Mamie, est-ce qu'il y avait Internet à ton époque ?
English:     Grandma, was there Internet in your time?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Non ! Avant, il y avait rarement l'électricité dans les maisons.
English:     No! Before, there was rarely electricity in houses.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Comment tu pouvais vivre sans Internet ?
English:     How were you able to live without the internet?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Sans l'électricité, tout était plus difficile.
English:     Without electricity, everything was more difficult.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu ne pouvais pas parler au téléphone ?
English:     You didn't use to be able to talk on the phone?
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Non. Avant, on écrivait des lettres.
English:     No. Before, we wrote letters.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Quand j'étais un jeune homme...
To make the imparfait , start from the nous form, like nous écrivons and nous pouvons . Then drop the ‑ons , and then add the endings listed below!

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( pouvoir)          
je I                      | pouv ais was able to     
tu you                    | pouv ais were able to    
il / elle he / she        | pouv ait was able to     
nous we                   | pouv ions were able to   
vous you all              | pouv iez were able to    
ils / elles they          | pouv aient were able to  
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Avant, nous écrivions des lettres.
English:     Before, we used to write letters.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Ongoing actions… in the past!
To say things like I was talking instead of I talked , follow this pattern:

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( parler)           
je                        | parl ais                 
tu                        | parl ais                 
il / elle                 | parl ait                 
nous                      | parl ions                
vous                      | parl iez                 
ils / elles               | parl aient               
-------------

Discuss games and media

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Cette vidéo est trop drôle.
English:     This video is too funny.

English:     Can you show it to me?

French:      Oui, je vais t'envoyer le lien.
English:     Yes, I'm going to send you the link.
----------------------

English:     My son likes this game so I'm going to give it to him.
----------------------

French:      Si tu veux ce magazine, je te le donne.
English:     If you want this magazine, I'll give it to you.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'ai téléchargé une application très sympa.
English:     I downloaded a very nice application.

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
You can use two, too!
Remember that pronouns like le , leur , me , and so on come before the verb . And sometimes, you'll use not only one, but two of these pronouns!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je lui donne le livre.
English:     I givehim/her the book.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je le lui donne.
English:     I giveit to him/her.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je leur donne la pomme.
English:     I givethem the apple.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je la leur donne.
English:     I giveit to them.
----------------------
Notice that le , la , and les come before lui or leur !

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je lui donne la pomme. Je la lui donne.
English:     I giveher the apple. I giveit to her.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
And for me?
Even though lui and leur go after le , la , and les , the pronouns me , te , nous , and vous , come before!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je te le donne.
English:     I giveit to you.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ils vous les offrent.
English:     They offerthem to you.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Vous me les prêtez.
English:     You lendthem to me.
----------------------

Make plans to go out

Let's meet up!
Retrouver means to meet up with someone! But how about if you're saying people are all meeting up with each other? Then you add a pronoun like se .

A change in me
We've seen how être is used with verbs to express some sort of movement in the past, like in Elle est allée .
You can also use être with verbs that show a change in someone's state of being (or a lack of change!) Some examples are mourir , naître , devenir , rester .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous sommes restés à Paris pendant trois semaines.
English:     We stayed in Paris for three weeks.

Make transit plans

How are you with geography?
To say that something is in the north, south, east or west of a place, you can use the word dans .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Dans le nord du Canada, il fait très froid.
English:     Innorthern Canada, it is very cold.
----------------------
But to say that something is to the north, south, east, or west of somewhere, you can use forms of à !

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      L'Océan Atlantique est à l'est des États‑Unis.
English:     The Atlantic Ocean is east of the United States.

========================================
TITLE: Unit 24 Guidebook
========================================
Explore grammar tips and key phrases for this unit


------------------------------
KEY PHRASES
------------------------------
Use commands

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Dépêchez-vous, ou le bus va partir sans vous !
English:     Hurry up, or the bus is going to leave without you!
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Garons-nous là-bas !
English:     Let's park over there!
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Non, ne vous garez pas sur ce parking.
English:     No, don't park in this parking lot.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Attention, ne te perds pas.
English:     Careful, don't get lost.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ne te lève pas trop vite.
English:     Don't stand up too quickly.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Lève-toi parce que le train va arriver dans la gare.
English:     Stand up because the train is going to arrive at the station.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Ne te gare pas ici, c'est interdit !
We've seen that Ne mange pas ! means Don't eat! But when telling someone not to do something with verbs like se perdre or se garer , you need to add a vous or te in there.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ne te perds pas !
English:     Don't get lost!
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ne vous garez pas là !
English:     Don't park there!
----------------------
For the sentences with te , remember to drop the s on the end of ‑er verbs like se dépêch er .

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ne te dépêche pas !
English:     Don't hurry!
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Changes of state in the past!
When talking about the past, verbs that indicate motion or change of state use être instead of avoir . If the subject is feminine , add an ‑e . If the subject is plural , add an ‑s !

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( mourir )          
je                        | suis mort (e)            
tu                        | es mort (e)              
il / elle                 | est mort (e)             
nous                      | sommes mort (e)s         
vous                      | êtes mort (e)s           
ils / elles               | sont mort (e)s           
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Oui, j'ai acheté une petite table carrée pour le salon.
English:     Yes, I bought a small square table for the living room.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ces tasses sont très jolies.
English:     These mugs are very pretty.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Si tu aimes ces tasses, achète-les.
English:     If you like these mugs, buy them.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ce tapis est tout neuf.
English:     This rug is brand new.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Mets la nouvelle lampe sur la table et allume-la.
English:     Put the new lamp on the table and turn it on.
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Achète‑les !
When giving commands like Buy them ! or Call her ! , the French pronouns le , la , and les are tied to the verb with a hyphen!

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Prends‑le !
English:     Takeit!
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Appelle‑la !
English:     Callher!
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Achète‑les !
English:     Buythem!
----------------------
But if you're telling someone not to do something, le , la , and les come before the verb.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ne le prends pas !
English:     Don't takeit!
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ne l'appelle pas !
English:     Don't callher!
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ne les achète pas !
English:     Don't buythem!
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ne le mets pas ici !
English:     Don't putithere!
----------------------

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Ce sont de bons gâteaux
We've seen that some adjectives go before the word that they describe.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      C'est un bon livre.
English:     It is agoodbook.
----------------------
We've also seen that you need to put des before plural nouns !

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'achète des livres.
English:     I buy books.
----------------------
And if both these happen together? Use de before the adjective instead of des !

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je porte de nouvelles chaussures.
English:     I am wearingnewshoes.
----------------------

English:     They will come back from vacation on August twelfth.

------------------------------
TIP
------------------------------
Je penserai à toi !
In French, verbs have a future form! For ‑er and ‑ir verbs (like chant er and fin ir ), you'll start with the infinitive then use these endings:

--- Table ---
verb parler               | verb finir               
je parler ai              | je finir ai              
tu parler as              | tu finir as              
il / elle parler a        | il / elle finir a        
nous parler ons           | nous finir ons           
vous parler ez            | vous finir ez            
ils / elles parler ont    | ils / elles finir ont    
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ils partiront à la plage.
English:     They will go to the beach.

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( vendre)           
je I                      | vendr ai will sell       
tu you                    | vendr as will sell       
il / elle he / she        | vendr a will sell        
nous we                   | vendr ons will sell      
vous you all              | vendr ez will sell       
ils / elles they          | vendr ont will sell      
-------------

Let’s talk about Future Tense!
To talk about the future, follow this pattern:

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( parler )          
je                        | parler ai                
tu                        | parler as                
il / elle                 | parler a                 
nous                      | parler ons               
vous                      | parler ez                
ils / elles               | parler ont               
-------------
Some verbs have an irregular base, but still use the same endings.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Je serai heureux.
English:     I will be happy.

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous aurons temps.
English:     We will have time.

J'y pense tout le temps !

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Tu y penses.
English:     You thinkabout it.

TIP
------------------------------
J'en ai besoin !

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      J'en rêve.
English:     I dreamabout it.​

English:     We are afraidof this exam.
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Nous en avons peur.​
English:     We are afraidof it.​
----------------------

--- Example Phrase ---
French:      Ils ont besoin d'aide. Ils en ont besoin.
English:     They needhelp. They needit.

When you want to say something politely, you can use verb forms like tu voud rais , tu pour rais , and tu dev rais ! Take a look at the ending pattern:

--- Table ---
subject                   | verb ( pouvoir )         
je I                      | pour rais could          
tu you                    | pour rais could          
il / elle he / she        | pour rait could          
nous we                   | pour rions could         
vous you all              | pour riez could          
ils / elles they          | pour raient could        
-------------

--- Example Phrase ---
